Sports

International University Games 103

August 7 to August 26

Held in Germany, with participants from 12 countries

Eligibility limited to students under 27 years old

Japan will depart tomorrow; Chinese soccer may as well attend.

The fourth International University Athletics Competition will be held in Darmstadt, Germany, from August 7 this year. The venue is the sports field of the city's Industrial University, and the event is organized by the International Student Federation, which has already begun preparing everything. Participants include England, Germany, Japan, France, Italy, Belgium, Hungary, Egypt, Estonia, Switzerland, Romania, and Yugoslavia. Recently, Norway, Sweden, Finland, the Netherlands, the Czech Republic, Denmark, and Austria have also registered to participate. The chairman of the conference is Mr. Grudius, the German Foreign Minister, and the president is Dr. Olan, the president of the Industrial University. The chairman of the General Affairs Committee is currently determined to be Mr. Soling Geru, the physical education instructor of the Industrial University. The consultant of the conference is currently undertaking the task of Mayor Darmstadt Standard. The various departments of the competition are managed by the German Sports Association, and the chief referee is Mr. Baldo, who led the athletes to the East last year and participated in the China-Japan-Germany sports meet held in Liaoning. The conference will last for a total of ten days, from August 10 to August 26. At the same time, the city will also hold a 600th-anniversary celebration. Students from the Industrial University and other schools will hold lantern parades and concerts every night, and a grand fireworks display will be held on the banks of the Sezuka River to express their welcome to the international athletes. The Zeppellin airship will be dispatched to the city to provide sightseeing tours for the athletes from various countries. All preparatory matters are now in full swing. The eligibility for participating athletes is limited to university students under the age of 27. The competition events include track and field, swimming, netball, volleyball, soccer, baseball, and rowing. If it is winter, ice skating and skiing will be added. The conference is held every two years. The first was held in Warsaw in 1924, the second in Rome in 1926, and the third in Paris in 1928. In the last session, Germany won the championship with 157 points, France won the second place with 88 points, and England ranked third. Japan will officially send athletes to participate in this conference. England and France fear that they will be surpassed by Japan, because Japan's amazing achievements in the Far East have been shocking to Europe and the West. Japan has hopes of winning the second place in this international conference. Japan ranks second in the world in swimming and baseball. Japan ranks first in the world in women's track and field. In men's track and field, Yoshioka's 10.8 seconds in the 100 meters, 21.5 seconds in the 200 meters, Nakajima's 49 seconds in the 400 meters, Iwanaga's 15 seconds in the high jump, Sumiyoshi's Ito's 62 meters in the javelin, Oda's 7 meters in the long jump, and Nishida's 4.15 meters in the pole vault are all expected to be selected in the conference. Japan's entire team of athletes is about 100 people and is scheduled to depart from Tokyo on June 18, pass through Korea and the three northeastern provinces, and take the Trans-Siberian train to arrive in Darmstadt on August 2.

Since the eligibility for participating athletes is limited to students under the age of 27, if our country's university soccer team can be mixed into a strong lineup, it is not impossible to try to compete for the International Student Championship.

Japan Ministry of Education Promotes Physical Education Plan

Our Country's Authorities Should Quickly Reflect 104

Tokyo Communication: The Japanese Ministry of Education, in order to seek the rational development and control of physical education, issued instructions on November 26 last year to organize a Physical Education Council, widely hiring experienced and knowledgeable people from all over the country as special members to repeatedly hold meetings to discuss rational ways to promote physical education. The draft plan has been decided as follows:

(1) Draft Plan 105

Physical education is of great significance for invigorating the spirit of the people and enhancing physical fitness, and it is also of great importance to the progress of national life. For this reason, it is requested that officials and people concerned should cooperate with each other, adhere to the following guidelines and key points, and in view of the current situation, rationally promote physical education as a matter of urgency.

(1) In order to achieve the full development of national capabilities, it is necessary to abandon the disadvantages of emphasizing intellectual education and strive to popularize physical education.

(2) Study various sports at home and abroad, adopt the strengths and make up for the weaknesses, and pay special attention to cultivating the spirit of sports.

(3) It is necessary to base on scientific research, actively complete the rational guidance of physical education, and hope that the national physique will be improved and healthy.

(4) In order to improve the health of women and seek the excellence of the next generation of national physique, it is necessary to pay attention to promoting women's physical education.

(5) It is necessary to carefully prevent the associated disadvantages of physical education and strive for significant results to achieve the true purpose.

(II) Key Points 106

Regarding the Improvement of Physical Education Administrative Organs

(I) The Ministry of Education shall establish a Bureau of Physical Education, and local government school affairs departments shall establish a Section of Physical Education. Major cities shall also establish Physical Education Departments or Bureaus according to the same administrative system.

(II) The Ministry of Education shall appoint Physical Education Officers, and local governments shall appoint Physical Education Supervisors (in accordance with local treatment of civil servant regulations).

Regarding Physical Education Research

(I) Expand physical education research institutions, striving to enrich research on appropriate exercise standards and other rational guidance necessary for national customs, age, physical condition, occupation, etc., with more comprehensive and meticulous research.

(II) Universities, specialized schools, and other institutions shall establish sports medicine and sports psychology courses. The government shall actively encourage and provide necessary assistance for other scientific research related to sports.

(III) Establish health consultation centers for physical education and sports.

Regarding Institutions for Training Physical Education Instructors

(I) Emphasize and improve comprehensive sports fields, maintain close ties to enable constant practical sports science research, and establish physical education universities or well-equipped physical education specialized schools to cultivate outstanding physical education instructors.

(II) Improve existing training institutions to enhance instructors' knowledge in school and youth group physical education.

Regarding Physical Education in Schools and Youth Groups

(I) School authorities must provide genuine and meaningful guidance to students' physical education with understanding and sympathy.

(II) Strive to complete physical education facilities with public funds and employ appropriate instructors.

(III) Universities and higher specialized schools shall appoint supervisors to manage physical education.

(IV) Adjust the teaching time of intellectual subjects in higher specialized schools and secondary schools, increasing the number of class hours for various physical education activities.

(V) Change the gymnastics subject to physical education, enriching the content of teaching guidelines.

(VI) Allocate sufficient funds for physical education in each school and make it available for use.

(VII) Compile textbooks on physical education (for teachers).

(VIII) Focus on appropriate guidance and provide corresponding subsidies for youth group physical education activities.

Regarding Public Physical Education

(I) Workers in factories, mines, stores, etc., have a great need for health care; therefore, special attention should be paid to encouraging physical education.

(II) Government offices, companies, banks, factories, etc., shall appoint physical education instructors and equip sports fields to provide more opportunities for exercise.

(III) Strive for the development of physical education associations and clubs so that men, women, old, and young can often have the opportunity to engage in sports.

(IV) Encourage various outdoor and indoor sports fields, martial arts fields, and sports-related facilities such as mountain cabins. If necessary, consider methods of providing subsidies.

(V) Consider appropriate methods to open school sports fields for public use and engagement in physical education.

(VI) Within the limits of the administrator's authority, appoint appropriate instructors for sports fields.

Regarding Women's Physical Education

(I) Regarding women's physical education, women's self-awareness must first be fully awakened.

(II) Equip dedicated sports fields for women.

(III) The design, promotion, and implementation of physical education programs for women must be suitable for women's nature and pay attention to the full realization of their mission.

(IV) Women's sports should be led by qualified female instructors; therefore, efforts must be made to fully develop their qualifications.

Regarding Physical Education Organizations

(I) Various sports shall be organized into national groups, and individual groups shall form comprehensive physical education organizations (or committees) based on these individual groups.

(II) Local organizations at the prefecture and county level shall connect with national comprehensive organizations and various sports groups to promote physical education within the prefecture and county and to oversee physical education groups within their jurisdiction.

(III) Youth groups must strive to maintain close contact with general sports groups.

Regarding Athletic Competitions and Athletes

(I) Championship competitions must be conducted in accordance with the official physical education organizations or with their approval.

(II) Regarding the holding and participation in athletic meets, as well as the number of events and the distinction of sports, a certain policy must be established, and efforts should be made to encourage them based on the current situation.

(III) If admission fees are charged, a certain policy must be established regarding guidance and inspection.

(IV) The significance of guiding athletes must be clearly recognized, and efforts should be made for their healthy development.

(V) Athletes should undergo regular physical examinations and pay attention to their health.

(VI) Consider appropriate methods and strive to prevent the professionalization of athletes and other malpractices.

Regarding Physical Education Thought

(I) The meaning and effect of physical education should be further promoted to increase national understanding and popularize proper physical education thought.

Regarding the Meiji Jingu Outer Garden Sports Grounds

(I) Actively complete the construction of various sports fields in the Meiji Jingu Outer Garden, making it the center of Japanese physical education (Zeng Yanhua)

The Dalian Chinese Youth Association, to promote physical education, invites athletes from Dalian and Lushun to hold the Dalian Chinese Track and Field Games in Dalian at the beginning of each summer. The Premium Yesterday

600 Taels Left Customs 116

An unprecedented major change in foreign exchange occurred again yesterday. The shilling quotation was first reduced by one penny to one shilling and five pennies. The 25th exchange rate suddenly rose by 7.875 cents, calculated as one tael, four mace, one tael, four mace and one cent, seven-five. The US exchange rate fell by two yuan to only 34.75 yuan. People's Food is Becoming Increasingly Difficult 117

Rice Flour and Wheat Prices Rise Together

The Social Affairs Bureau Seeks to Level Prices

Recently, the price of wheat flour has been increasing day by day. The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau believes that the new wheat has been released on the market, and the price should have fallen. Such an abnormal situation, even if there is a relationship between gold prices, should not be so obvious. It is evident that unscrupulous merchants are disregarding government orders and manipulating food for profit. Yesterday, it was heard that the Bureau sent personnel to the Flour and Miscellaneous Grain Exchanges to investigate. It was found that although the Flour Exchange had decided to increase the evidence money and set a deadline for short delivery, the Bureau's committee believed that there was still room for discretionary increases. On the one hand, it also ordered the Miscellaneous Grain Exchange to do the same. The flour bulls this time were Shunfeng and Qingchangxin, two brokers who bought nearly 60,000 bags in the near term by the 14th, and even more in the long term, which was indeed suspected of manipulation.

Moreover, the rice price in the city, since the Social Affairs Bureau approved the relaxation of the maximum rice price limit of one yuan, was originally a temporary measure. Once the milling loss is reduced, it should be restored to below twenty yuan. However, according to reports, a small number of rice boats are secretly sabotaging the situation, and rice shops are also voluntarily posting prices in order not to be exposed. The Social Affairs Bureau believes that both the truth and falsehood should be thoroughly investigated and immediately summoned a certain Jin, an employee of the Changshu Rice Merchants Association stationed in Shanghai, to the bureau to add a warning and order him to investigate and report the matter truthfully without concealing it. In addition, from tomorrow, all prices for Changshu boats and trading shops should be reported to the Bureau by the Association on a daily basis. It was also found that a certain Yan, a large merchant in the South City, offered a price of 19.6 yuan for the rice from Tongli that he sold, which was also obviously exceeding the limited price of medium-quality rice. He was first ordered to reply clearly and then investigated.

Mr. Hu happened to be sending Mayor Zhang out, and he was met after being invited. He was tasked by Commander Zhang to come south to thank them. Furthermore, because his illness had not fully recovered, he would stay in Shanghai for recuperation and treatment. He would have to wait until he recovered from his illness before he could take up the position of Vice Minister of Health. Because he would have to work hard on his mission after taking office, he would have to fully rest in order to restore his health. As for Commander Zhang's eagerness for peace in the current situation, he is extremely willing to mediate so that weapons of war can be turned into jade and silk, and jointly develop the country. Because he has no important mission, there is no need to meet with Chairman Chiang for the time being. In the future, he may be summoned to meet at any time.

The Likin Abolition Committee

Progress of the Third Preparatory Meeting 120

Representatives from Five Provinces Have Registered

The Provinces Are Requesting Subsidies from the Ministry of Finance

Since the Ministry of Finance commissioned Counselor Li Jihong to come to Shanghai to preside over the National Likin Abolition Conference, the preparatory meeting has been held three times. Jia Shiyi, Director of the Tax Department of the Ministry of Finance, and Zhang Fuyun, Director of the Customs Administration, both came to Shanghai to attend. A reporter from the Continental Society visited a certain official who participated in the meeting yesterday and asked about the results of the meeting. According to him, there were more than ten representatives from provinces such as Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, and Hubei who attended the third preparatory meeting in Shanghai. All submitted various plans and opinions. Chairman Li Jihong used the method of discussing province by province to first present the contents of one province, including the current likin situation, the annual unified tax table, the steps to abolish likin, the plan to replace likin, and the special circumstances of each province. After detailed discussion, the opinions of the provinces were collectively viewed. The replacement tax after the abolition of likin can only offset a part of the current likin. The provinces are requesting subsidies from the Ministry of Finance for the funds that are insufficient for government expenditure. The Ministry of Finance cannot fully accept this point, nor can it completely reject it. It can only examine the tax revenue situation of each province to seek a legal replacement. When it is unavoidable, it can only be maintained internally and externally, and the Ministry of Finance will give discretionary subsidies to serve as a transition after the abolition of likin. Other methods will be formulated to jointly maintain the tax revenue and government expenditure of a province. The matter must be satisfactorily resolved. The formal date of the conference must be postponed until all the representatives from the provinces have gathered. A fourth preparatory meeting will have to be held before the conference. The date of the conference will be determined by the meeting.

Problem of Recovering Telephone Concessions 122

Tax Association Sent Letter to Edward Yesterday

Chen Shiguang Will Meet with Consular Leaders

The Shanghai Renters' Association of Chinese Taxpayers sent a letter to Mr. Edward, the General Manager of the Public Concession Board, yesterday. The letter said: "The lack of speed and efficiency of the Shanghai Chinese and Foreign Telephone Company has long been well known to your Board, and the company itself is aware of its shortcomings. Therefore, recently, it has been proceeding with the sale and connection to other companies. However, telephone is a public utility and is related to transportation everywhere. The convenience of transportation cannot be completed if the management and system of telephones in one place are not the same as in other places. From the perspective of the world, telephone services are mostly operated by the state and municipalities. Our country adopts the state-run method, then the franchised telephone business should be acquired and managed by our government, so that the use of telephones is extensive and the benefits of being accessible everywhere are received. Moreover, since the company is in the process of selling, in order to respect Our national sovereignty, Your Board will certainly assist in transferring the franchise right of telephones in the concession to Our government. Please note and show your willingness to assist."

The Ministry of Communications has sent a letter to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to seriously negotiate with the envoys of the United Kingdom and France on the recovery of the telephone concession. In addition to issuing a declaration, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs also sent a telegram to the envoys of the United Kingdom and France, ordering the British and French consuls stationed in Shanghai to negotiate with personnel appointed by the Ministry of Communications to discuss the recovery methods. Chen Shiguang and Liu Yunfang, the two directors of the External Affairs Office stationed in Shanghai, were ordered to send a letter to the consular leaders to seriously negotiate. According to Director Chen Shiguang, Minister Wai ordered him to first consult with Mr. Ke Yinhan, the American Consul General who led the meeting, and exchange opinions. There was no order to send a letter to negotiate. He is now preparing to visit the consular leaders. Once he has met and discussed, he will present it to the External Affairs Office for verification.

Impact of Gold Market on the Shipping Industry 123

Few Passengers and Goods

In recent years, because of the fierce competition in the shipping industry among the United Kingdom, the United States, and Japan, all countries have gone all out to compete for shipping rights. As a result, there are dozens of foreign ships sailing on the Shanghai, Hong Kong, Japan, and American routes. Japan has put in the most effort. There are as many as six foreign ships regularly traveling and sailing by the Nippon Yusen Kaisha alone. At that time, the Pacific route war attracted the attention of countries around the world. Unfortunately, recently, due to the soaring price of gold and the disastrous fall in the exchange rate, all industries have been greatly affected. At the same time, import and export business has plummeted, resulting in no goods for ships to carry and making it impossible to maintain operations. The Board of Directors of the Nippon Yusen Kaisha has decided that, in order to remedy the current difficulties, the Tientsin Maru will be temporarily suspended. If there is no change next month, the Chunyo Maru, etc., will be suspended one after another to reduce losses. The Tientsin Maru arrived in Shanghai from Hong Kong yesterday, stayed for only two hours, and then set sail for Yokohama to suspend operations. In addition, several foreign companies from the United Kingdom, the United States, and France will also suspend operations within the month. This kind of decline is unprecedented in the shipping industry.

Annual Meeting of the Jinpu Railway Yesterday 130

Report on Last Year's Business Performance

The Board of Directors of the Jinpu Railway held its annual regular meeting yesterday (the 16th) at 3:00 PM in the Railway Administration Office, in accordance with the loan contract. The meeting included a report on the previous year's business performance and discussions on various future issues. According to regulations, three representatives from the Anglo-Chinese Corporation and Liu Weichi, Director, and Luo, Section Chief, from the railway side attended. Director Liu, as chairman, first reported that both passenger and freight traffic on the railway had increased significantly during the 18th year, especially passenger traffic. As a result, the net profit for the past year was higher than ever before, which was gratifying. However, while revenue had increased, expenses for employee salaries and urgent infrastructure construction were also substantial. The sharp rise in gold prices this year had a significant impact on the railway's foreign orders for locomotives and materials, as well as on loan repayments and interest payments. Therefore, greater efforts were needed to further develop the railway's business. Liu also reported that the vehicles ordered from abroad last year had been arriving successively, and that the train operation situation would be improved and the travel time between Jinan and Shanghai would be shortened once all the locomotives arrived, in order to improve efficiency. Regarding rumors that the railway planned to use the Boxer Indemnity to purchase 18 locomotives from foreign countries, he stated that this was absolutely not true.

China Aviation Transport Company

Negotiations on Amending the Contract 131

New Contract Expected to be Signed Next Week

It has been reported in the newspapers that Sun Ke, the Minister of Railways, previously formed the China Aviation Transport Company with American businessmen to fly daily between Shanghai and Wuhan. However, the contract was quite unfavorable to the Chinese side, and the China Aviation Transport Company was transferred to the Ministry of Communications. Wang Boqun, the Minister of Communications, immediately sent representatives to negotiate with the American representatives in Beijing to amend the contract. This matter has been quiet recently, but according to sources from the Ministry of Communications yesterday, negotiations are still underway in Beijing. A large part of the new contract has been finalized. The content stipulates a capital of three thousand

Page 14

ten thousand yuan, with the Chinese side accounting for 55% and the American side accounting for 45%. Future personnel, administration, and the establishment of the board of directors will be based on this ratio. The company will be reorganized according to Chinese company regulations. As for the bonds paid monthly by the Chinese side to the American side due to the constraints of the previous contract, this was the most contentious point in the negotiations between the two sides. The American side has repeatedly changed its representatives for this reason. The two sides have now agreed in principle that the bonds paid by the Chinese side will be used as the Chinese side's new capital, and the bonds received by the American side will also be used as the American side's capital, or they will be offset against each other. One of these methods will be chosen in the future. According to Minister Wang, the new contract is expected to be signed next week and will be announced after being submitted to the Executive Yuan for approval.

A conflict arose with wounded soldiers over the competition for donkeys, leading to a mutual brawl. Several soldiers and Japanese students were injured, two of the Japanese students more seriously. Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway's Appeal for Rice Inspection 138

The Predicament of Bridge No. 34

Recently, rice merchants from Southern Jiangsu carrying rice to Shanghai via the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway route encountered troops stationed at Bridge No. 34. The rice boats were ordered to stop and inspected, with troops boarding each cabin to check. The rice merchants, eager to reach Shanghai to sell their goods, presented letters of consignment from inland rice merchants to Shanghai rice customers, requesting prompt release. However, their requests were ignored, and they were detained for a day. The rice boat of Ding Jisheng inquired about the reason for the inspection and argued with them, whereupon he was beaten and injured, and the boat was also detained for a day before being released. After the rice boats arrived in Shanghai, they reported the situation to the Southern Jiangsu Rice Merchants Association. Yesterday, the association convened a meeting of rice merchants, at which Ding Jisheng and others reported on the inspection by the troops stationed at Bridge No. 34. They were ordered to stop for inspection, and could not leave immediately after the inspection. The tide was rapid there, and when they pleaded, they were ignored and detained for half a day or a day. Therefore, boats behind them were afraid to pass through the area and mostly turned back. Now, the boatmen must wait for the inspection to be cancelled before they can carry goods. After discussions, the rice merchants decided that Bridge No. 34 was the only way for rice boats to reach Shanghai, and they did not know which department the troops stationed there belonged to. At a time when rice prices are high and the source is scarce, further inspection and delay would lead to a shortage of goods in the Shanghai market, affecting the people's food supply. Therefore, they decided to send a letter to the Chamber of Commerce, requesting it to ask the authorities to instruct the troops at Bridge No. 34 to cancel the inspection of rice boats, and to advise the rice boats in Shanghai not to panic and to continue carrying goods as usual from the interior. They will also send a letter to the rice businesses in various inland ports to inform them of the situation.

Cotton Industry Association Requests Improvement of Cotton Inspection 139

The Shanghai Chinese Cotton Industry Association petitioned the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, stating that it was appealing for a thorough reform of the cotton inspection office, recognizing the status of merchants and farmers, in order to alleviate the suffering of cotton merchants. It believed that the Ministry's intention in establishing the inspection office was to improve cotton production and assist in business operations. However, after the establishment of inspection bureaus in various places, years had passed without any progress. Cotton merchants in Hankou had repeatedly appealed, expressing their deep pain and shedding tears. If the Ministry did not promptly reform, it feared that cotton merchants would become fish in a dried-up rut. The association, with its related responsibilities, dared not remain silent and specially presented the following points: cotton traders, manufacturers, and foreign merchants could all directly purchase from producing areas, and farmers could also sell to manufacturers in marketing areas. Now, the inspection bureau only inspects a portion of the cotton merchants, and does not advise on cotton purchased by manufacturers themselves. For cotton merchants, it does not matter whether the cotton is sold overseas or domestically. Once the packaging factory is used, inspection begins. Fellow cotton merchants in Hankou have already spoken in detail about their suffering. It is a pity that cotton merchants have complied with the Ministry's orders to the point where they are unable to operate, but cotton production has not improved. Manufacturers reduce prices to buy low-quality goods, and farmers sell to manufacturers instead of cotton merchants, so low-quality goods can still be sold smoothly without hindrance. Only cotton merchants are left to sit and wait for death. Is this the Ministry's original intention in establishing the inspection bureau? Hankou, Ningbo, and other places are neither producing areas nor direct ports for overseas sales, so there is no need to establish inspection bureaus there. If they have already been established, then they should start by inspecting goods transported for overseas sales, and for goods transported domestically, it seems appropriate to freely request inspection in accordance with Article 3 of the Ministry's Inspection Regulations. In other words, there is no need for a certificate to report transportation to domestic ports. The restrictions on traders due to Article 4 of the Ministry's Inspection Regulations prevent them from trading, so manufacturers procure and transport cotton themselves in the producing areas. With a single order from the Ministry, the livelihood of cotton merchants is suddenly gone. Moreover, the inspection bureau has not been in operation for a year, and it is questionable whether the water content limit of 182 to 15 has already achieved considerable results. On January 1 of this year, without consideration, an order was issued to change the water content standard to 12 to 14 percent, and it is planned to change it to 11 to 13 percent on January 1 of next year. This kind of method that does not seek the root but only cares about the branches is truly frustrating and leaves us with no way to appeal. Furthermore, the soil and climate of Chinese cotton are different from those of Indian cotton, and there is also the difference between herbaceous and woody cotton. We cannot simply rely on others' superficial experience and talk about improvement. In short, improving cotton production should fundamentally be done by rectifying the producing areas, and the Ministry cannot shirk its responsibility for the difficulties of Jiangsu merchants. It is hoped that the Ministry will recognize the status of merchants and farmers, assess the inspection bureaus in various places in order, and strive for thorough reform. The lifeline of cotton merchants is dependent on this.

Zhu Qinglan Investigates Recent Conditions of the Shaanxi Disaster 145

The tragic deaths of disaster victims in the Shaanxi disaster have been reported repeatedly in Chinese and foreign newspapers. Last winter, there was continuous heavy snow. Due to the lack of seeds, only one-tenth of the area in the province was sown with winter wheat. Subsequently, farmers mostly supplemented by planting peas. Lantian, Yaoxian, and other counties had particularly large plantings. It is now reported that the planted beans are growing an inch or so in height, and green insects are breeding rapidly. There are not enough methods to catch and kill them. They eat the bean leaves as silkworms eat mulberry leaves. In an instant, they eat everything. Wherever they pass, everything becomes withered. Disaster upon disaster can be said to be cruel. Recently, Sun Jun Weidong, the representative of the Shaanxi Relief Association stationed in Beijing and Shanghai, received a telegram from Shaanxi reporting on Zhu Qinglan's investigation of the disaster conditions in Shaanxi. The telegram is reproduced as follows: Zhu Qinglan went to Ganyang and Liquan in western Shaanxi to investigate the disaster conditions. According to the investigation, the severely affected areas in western Shaanxi are uninhabited, and the lightly affected areas have also reduced the original population by 50% to 60% or 70% to 80%. From west of Xianyang County City, passing through Liquan and Qianxian, to the boundary of Yongshou County, an area of about 200 miles wide, no wheat seedlings were seen. Relief in the disaster area should be provided simultaneously with seeds, draft cattle, and emergency relief. In addition, epidemics are prevalent in various disaster areas, and disaster victims are dying from either starvation or disease. In a village in Liquan, it was seen that a household with a total of 49 family members had already starved to death 36. Of the remaining 13, nine are sick and all suffer from epidemics. Zhu said that after returning to Tianjin, in addition to raising large sums of relief money, he plans to ask major pharmacies in Tianjin to donate 100,000 doses of plague-preventing pills, Ten Drops of Water, Lonicera and Forsythia Detoxification Pills, Forsythia Powder, and Baodan pills for distribution in Shaanxi for relief efforts.

Six Articles of Regulations for the Defense Corps 147

Promulgated by the Consolidation Committee

The team leaders of the Defense Corps in the South Shanghai and Zhabei districts of Shanghai Special Municipality recently received six articles of regulations issued by the Consolidation Committee through the Corps Headquarters, and immediately announced them to the members of each team to comply with. The announcement is recorded below for general information: Case No. 109 of the Corps Headquarters's instruction stated that six articles of regulations ordered by the Defense Corps Consolidation Committee have been forwarded to the team for promulgation and should be complied with. The regulations are as follows: (1) Corps members shall not wear uniforms except during training and other official duties. (2) Corps members wearing military uniforms without wearing armbands will be considered as disrupting discipline. (3) Corps members wearing civilian clothes while carrying handguns will be considered as wandering around with weapons. (4) Corps members who purchase firearms without first reporting to the association for approval will be considered as privately purchasing military supplies. (5) Corps members who arrest bandits must not fire their guns without the order of a superior. Even in cases of legitimate self-defense, they must not act excessively. If the detainees cause casualties, they will be considered as intentional homicide. (6) Corps members who arrest bandits should cooperate with the police. The captured bandits or suspects must be immediately sent to the nearby district office for transfer to the Public Security Bureau for investigation. Violators will be considered as making arrests without authorization.

Local News

Mitsui & Co. Lacks Legal Personhood 149

Million-Dollar Debt Case Temporarily Suspended

Mitsui & Co. Has Not Registered with the National Government

Therefore, It Cannot Obtain the Rights of a Legal Person

Lawyer Zhang Rongxi's Unique Insight

Judge Ying Shi Proposes Two Solutions

He Gengxing, a compradore of the hardware department of the Japanese Mitsui & Co., opened Hongyu Hardware Store at No. 15 Renheli, Tianzhutang Street, in the French Concession, selling Mitsui's hardware products. Therefore, Mitsui & Co. is the most affected by He Gengxing's current debt and escape. It is reported that the amount of owed goods has reached more than one million, which is a huge loss in recent years. He's whereabouts have been unknown for a month since his escape. His Hongyu business has been controlled by other creditors and the French Concession Mixed Court has ordered personnel to be dispatched for liquidation. Most of the goods owed to Mitsui & Co. are guaranteed by Hong Cangting and others. Hong is also a guarantor in the contract for the sale of hardware signed with the Japanese head of Mitsui & Co. The contract was established in December of the year before last for a period of one year. Last year, after the expiration, both parties agreed to continue the validity period for another year, and Hong's guarantee responsibility was extended accordingly. Now Mitsui & Co. has filed a lawsuit against He in the Special District Local Court, and Hong is listed as the second defendant. Judge Ying Shi opened the court to hear three cases yesterday morning, including two cases of goods totaling tens of thousands of dollars, and the other was a case of bills. Before He fled, he successively paid Mitsui promissory notes totaling more than 39,250 taels of silver. Some of them were due, but when they were exchanged at the bank, not a penny was received. After investigation, those that were not due were all equal to waste paper. The company then filed a lawsuit requesting that He Gengxing be ordered to repay. If he cannot repay, the guarantor should be responsible. Hong, who lives at No. 102 Zhoushan Road, Hongkou, learned of the lawsuit and hired lawyer Zhang Rongxi to represent him. Other guarantors also hired lawyers to represent them. First, Okamoto, the Japanese lawyer of the plaintiff Mitsui & Co., requested to publish a notice to summon He Gengxing. Then, Lawyer Zhang raised a question that had never been mentioned before, that the plaintiff was suing in the name of Mitsui & Co., which means that Mitsui claimed to be a legal person, but our country's law stipulates that if one wants to obtain the rights of a legal person, one should register with the government. He wondered whether Mitsui had registered with our country's government. Lawyer Okamoto immediately replied that Mitsui had not registered, and then continued to say that all foreign companies in this port have never registered, and no such issue has been raised in Sino-foreign lawsuits in the past. It can be said to be an innovation. On this point, my lawyer should ask for a ruling first. The judge then checked Article 30 of our country's current Civil Law and handed it to the lawyer to read, and said: In the past, during the era of the Mixed Court and the Provisional Court, no one mentioned this kind of problem, so no dispute arose. Now that our country has promulgated the law, we must of course abide by it. There are two solutions to this case: (1) to complete the registration; (2) to change the name of the plaintiff and have a natural person sue. A natural person is the head or manager of the plaintiff's company. However, the registration may take a long time. In order to expedite the case and avoid delays, it would be quicker to change to a natural person to sue. Okamoto said, suppose the plaintiff follows the instruction to apply for registration with the Chinese Ministry of Industry and Commerce, will the case be suspended during this period? The judge said yes. The lawyer then asked how long the registration would take. The judge said that this was not something the court should know, but the court had now clearly indicated two solutions. If the plaintiff decides to change to sue in the name of a natural person, they only need to correct the complaint. The opposing lawyer Zhang then expressed that the qualification of a natural person is still not suitable for this case, and said that if the plaintiff can apply for registration according to law, there will be no obstacles in diplomatic terms, and it should not be delayed for long. Lawyer Okamoto then requested that the case be adjourned for seven days for consideration, and asked to see Hong Cangting's power of attorney authorizing Zhang Rongxi to handle the case. After finishing, he stood up and claimed that the seal of Hong on the power of attorney was inconsistent with the seal of Hong on the guarantee contract. This should be noted. Lawyer Zhang stated that Hong had not only one seal, although they were not the same style, but it did not matter. Judge Ying also said that this point was not a problem, and with Lawyer Zhang's reputation, he would not appear in court without being entrusted. He told Okamoto not to worry too much, and then instructed that the request for a seven-day adjournment was too short. For the sake of the plaintiff's interests, the consideration period should be extended to facilitate the collection of evidence. It was decided to reschedule the hearing to the morning of June 28, and ordered that the announcement draft for He Gengxing's publication and the public fee for selecting a special agent for him be submitted to the case for approval. Therefore, the two cases of Mitsui & Co.'s lawsuit against He were also postponed to June 28 for a joint hearing due to the issue of the name of the lawsuit. According to the case of foreign companies suing Chinese people, foreign companies have been appearing in court for decades, and no one has ever expressed any objection. Now, after Zhang Rongxi's remarks, in the future, foreign merchants should sue Chinese people in the name of the head of the company. If they use the name of the company, they must first apply for registration with the Ministry of Industry and Commerce of the National Government. This is indeed a further step towards foreign countries after the recovery of legal rights.

Jiang Jing Steamer

Passenger Suicide Case 151

Claiming to be an Active-Duty Soldier

Returning from the Front Lines with Many Sighs

Disappeared in Zhenjiang Late at Night

Three Letters of Testament Found in the Cabin

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Jiang Jing steamer had a tragic suicide incident in which a passenger went missing on its voyage from Shanghai to Hankou. The information obtained is recorded as follows:

Passenger's Background: When the Jiang Jing steamer left Shanghai for work, a passenger came to the ship to buy a ticket. The young man, wearing a military uniform and only 28 years old, named Liu Dingpan, specified that he wanted to buy a single room in the first-class cabin when he boarded the ship. He didn't want to live with anyone, saying that he was from Hunan and currently held a military position in the headquarters. This time, he was going to Wuhan. The ship's waiter opened Room 6 of the large dining room for him to stay alone.

The Ship Moves: After the ship set sail, Liu Dingpan closed the door in Cabin 6 to write and buried himself in writing. Occasionally, when the waiter entered, he hid the book he was writing. The waiter and others did not pay attention at first. He wrote a letter in the cabin for about a day and a half. When the ship arrived in Zhenjiang and docked, the passenger began to open the cabin and leave the ship.

Missing Late at Night: When the ship arrived in Zhenjiang, it had to stop at the dock as usual. Liu Dingpan suddenly went out at this time, and did not instruct the waiter when he left the ship. The crew and others did not know until the next morning when the Jing steamer set off from Zhenjiang to Nanjing, and Liu Dingpan was not in the cabin. A thorough search of the entire ship was fruitless, and suddenly it was reported that he was missing.

Letters of Testament Discovered: The waiter went to the entrance of Cabin 6 and saw a letter of testament thrown on the ground. He picked it up and looked at it. It was thrown by the passenger Liu, saying that there were three letters in the cabin, please forward them according to the writing. The waiter went in and immediately took three letters from the table, one to the shipowner, one to the compradore, and one to the military law department of the headquarters, and one to his uncle. The letter to the shipowner said that he had recently returned from the front lines and felt that there was no hope for the future due to certain feelings, so he had the idea of ​​being tired of the world and committed suicide. The other two letters also asked to convey his regards, etc.

Two Letters Taken to Beijing: The shipowner and others sent this letter to the resident military police along with the remaining two letters to Beijing. Because he was an active-duty soldier, the letters were transferred to the Capital Garrison Headquarters for verification. There were no belongings in the cabin, leaving a hat, a washbasin, and six silver dollars, which he wrote to give to the waiter as a reward. Everyone expected that Liu left the ship that night and decided to jump into the Yangtze River to commit suicide when people were unprepared, but his body has not been found yet.

Husband and Concubine Allowed to Sever Ties 166

Zhang Aibao, a young woman from Nanxiang, is now 24 years old. Her husband, Zhang Ahu, died of illness on June 21 last year, leaving behind a three-year-old orphan girl. A widow lives in poverty. Han Yongru, the owner of the Gonghe Bamboo Cage Store on Bailinan Road, Caojiadu (also from Nanxiang, 49 years old), wanted to take her as a concubine. He hired someone to arrange a marriage and called Zhang Libo, Zhang Aibao's aunt from Nanxiang, to draw up a document to remarry Aibao to Han Yongru as a concubine, and stated in the document that Zhang Yongru would be responsible for Zhang Libo's support and funeral. This was in October last year. On May 11 this year, Zhang Aibao ran out alone because she could not bear the abuse and pleaded with lawyer Wang Xiangu to publish a statement to sever the relationship. At the same time, she also asked lawyer Wang to file a lawsuit with the local court requesting permission to sever the relationship. Her words roughly stated that after the plaintiff's husband died of illness last summer, the defendant Han Yongru made up an excuse to continue the marriage, so he took all the cage tools with him to the door. After arriving at the door, he learned that the defendant was already in his fifties and the plaintiff was only 24 years old. Even his children and daughters-in-law were older than the plaintiff. Moreover, the defendant still had a wife and did not provide food and clothing on weekdays, forcing the plaintiff to work. If she did not do it well, she would be beaten and scolded like a cow or a horse. She had no choice but to leave alone. In such a situation, it was difficult to grow old together, so she asked to sever the relationship. Yesterday morning, Judge Zhao Zhenhai specially opened the Tenth Court to hear the plaintiff Zhang Aibao's complaint and said that he requested to recover all the cage tools. (Question) Is there an inventory of the cage tools being pursued and how much are they worth? (Answer) Approximately one hundred yuan or so. The defendant Han Yongru confessed that he was 49 years old and from Nanxiang. He would not object to her severing the relationship, but we spent a total of 141 yuan on repayment and Huifang. As for all the cage tools, they are kept by his aunt. (Question) Is she a concubine? (Answer) Yes. (Question) Is there any evidence? (Answer) Yes. Then he presented a contract for the court to read. (Question) Who is Zhang Libo on the contract? (Answer) Aibao's aunt. The contract stated that I would take care of her in her old age. After the judge obtained the confession, he mediated the reconciliation in court and ordered the plaintiff to pay the defendant 30 yuan to allow the severance. Both parties expressed their willingness. At this point, the plaintiff's lawyer stood up and requested that the part of the cage tool pursuit be withdrawn. The judge then ordered Zhang Libo to come to the case and instructed, "Your daughter-in-law Zhang Aibao has severed the relationship with Han Yongru. The previous old-age support contract issued by Han Yongru should be invalidated." He then drew up a reconciliation record and ordered both parties to sign and leave the court.

A Woman, Looking Haggard, Attempts to Throw Herself into the River 167

She had stayed one night at the Shenzhou Hotel

When questioned, her answers were vague

Yesterday morning around 10 a.m., a woman, appearing to be in her early twenties, with short-cut hair, wearing a light gray floral serge qipao, flesh-colored stockings, and high-heeled leather shoes, and looking haggard, hailed a boat at the Jinliyuan Wharf of the China Merchants Bureau at the northern end of the 16th Pier, saying she wanted to cross the river. The boatman, noticing her sorrowful expression, paid close attention. Not far from the wharf, the woman suddenly moved to the front of the boat, facing the river as if to throw herself in. The boatman stopped her. At that moment, Huabu No. 15 of the Water Police Station was patrolling nearby and witnessed the scene. He questioned her, but she burst into tears. He took her to the police station and asked her name, age, and place of origin, but she did not answer any of the questions. Finally, she took a pen and wrote on paper, "Zhu, from this province," and other words. Her handwriting was delicate, as if she had received a higher education. She then spoke fluent Mandarin, claiming that her father was a very well-known person in society and asking to be excused for not being able to tell the truth. She requested to be taken to the Huangpu Wharf immediately. As soon as she finished speaking, she suddenly asked to be taken to the North Railway Station instead, because her home was in Suzhou. The police station staff, finding her words untruthful, asked if she suffered from a mental illness. The woman then laughed through her tears. They found a hotel bill from the Shenzhou Hotel on her person, stating "Mr. Zhu stayed in room 218 on June 15th, 1 dollar and 20 cents for one day, 50 cents for Western food, and 17 cents for small expenses." Seeing a lead to follow, the head of the police station telephoned the hotel. The hotel responded that last night (the 15th), a fashionable woman did indeed bring two pieces of luggage and rented that room. She provided a luggage receipt at the time and stayed one night. She left this morning, and nothing else was known. The head of the police station then asked the woman where the luggage receipt was, and she said it had been mailed to her brother to retrieve the luggage. The head of the police station, believing that she did not want to reveal the truth and must have some unspeakable secret, ordered the detective to transfer her to the local court for disposition.

Verification of Death by Poisoning of a Wine Shop Employee 169

Lin Jingluo, a Cantonese employee of the Xinfeng Wine Shop at No. 9, 17th Pier, Guangzhou, Guangdong, was ordered last year by the shop owner to bring 100 jars of wine worth 2,000 yuan to Shanghai for sale. After Lin sold the wine and obtained the money, he did not remit it back to the shop but instead spent it with Zhu Hanzhen, a prostitute at No. 603, Renzhi Lane, North Sichuan Road. Before long, he ran out of money and had no face to return to his hometown. Yesterday morning at around half past midnight, he attempted suicide by poisoning himself. The brothel owner discovered him and sent him to the hospital, but he had taken too much poison and died. The Hongkou police station dispatched Huabu No. 144 to send Lin's body to the forensic examination office on Fei Lun Road. Yesterday morning, Xu, the prosecutor from the Special District Court, arrived at the office to verify the cause of death. Zhu Hanzhen stated that she was a prostitute from Guangdong, 18 years old, working at No. 630, North Sichuan Road, and that she had known the deceased for some time. He came to her house and poisoned himself, but she knew nothing about it. However, when the deceased came to her house, he said he had been beaten on North Jiangxi Road. Liang Yiwen stated that he was the manager of the Xinfeng Wine Shop, 52 years old, and that the deceased had no family. He would take possession of the body. Old Jiangyin, Big Jiangyin, Little Jiangyin Fight with Little Coppersmith 170

Axe fight ends with bloodshed

In Shanghai, there is a man nicknamed Old Jiangyin, who has two sons, the elder named Big Jiangyin and the younger named Little Jiangyin. Old Jiangyin used to be a boss of the Sanitation Bureau, earning a substantial monthly income. When Old Jiangyin grew old, his elder son Big Jiangyin inherited his father's business. Big Jiangyin has a wife and a concubine. His wife lives in Dafu Lane, Fumin Road, in the city, and his concubine lives outside the Great South Gate. The younger son, Little Jiangyin, has no occupation and hangs out with gangsters, extorting money for a living. He has borrowed countless times from his brother and sister-in-law. The day before yesterday, he borrowed another ten yuan from his sister-in-law. This was known by Little Coppersmith, a follower of his elder brother Big Jiangyin, who knew that Little Jiangyin had extorted twenty yuan somewhere yesterday and was now borrowing from his brother again, which was considered greedy and insatiable. He informed Big Jiangyin's wife of the situation, who then questioned Little Jiangyin. Little Jiangyin was furious and found out that Little Coppersmith had stirred up trouble. He gathered more than ten gangsters, each carrying axes and other weapons, to seek revenge on Little Coppersmith. Little Coppersmith also gathered more than ten fellow brothers to resist. Around 11 p.m. the night before last, the two sides fought each other with weapons in front of Dafu Lane. Big Jiangyin also joined the fight to help his follower against his brother. As a result, Big Jiangyin was hit in the right shoulder with an axe, with a wound about three inches deep. Little Coppersmith was also slashed in the arm, covered in blood. Two people from Little Jiangyin's side were also injured by people from Little Coppersmith's side. When the police arrived, the people on Little Jiangyin's side had already dispersed. Only Big Jiangyin and Little Coppersmith (both injured) were still there. When questioned, Big Jiangyin claimed it was a family matter and there was no need to go to the police station. Each hired a car and went to the hospital for treatment.

Norwegian Ship Sinks Stone Carrier 171

Zhang Anxing Stone Works of Tongren Lane, Wusong Road, hired a wharf boat owned by Shen Yinsheng the other day. It was carrying 75 tons of stones on the Pujiang River, sailing north with the wind. At 11:35 a.m., it reached the vicinity of the Rihua Yarn Factory in Pudong. Due to the rising tide, it was about to turn to Puxi when the Norwegian merchant ship "Bmur" came from the north. The stone boat quickly tried to avoid it, but the ship was traveling very fast and instantly smashed the stone boat's hull. River water immediately flooded in. Because it was overloaded, even though the boatmen tried their best to return to Pudong, it was too late, and the boat and cargo sank to the bottom of the river. Fortunately, several boatmen were rescued unharmed. Currently, the Water Police Station, considering that the sunken ship's masts are high and obstruct ships entering and exiting the harbor, hired a wooden boat yesterday and anchored it at the accident site, hanging a green cloth flag to warn ships not to sail in that area to avoid danger. It is said that the ship and cargo losses amount to more than 2,300 yuan.

Four Thieves Arrested Afterward

Hong Daochang from Haizhou, a rickshaw puller residing at No. 29, Fengyu Lane, Hanzhong Road, Zhabei, was invaded by four thieves around 3 a.m. yesterday. The police went to the address and saw Fan Huiyu and Fan Xiaorong talking on the way to Meiyuan Road. Du identified them as the robbers and arrested them. Was Han Lijiang Beaten to Death? 173

Stealing Should Be Punished

Private Punishment Is Also Illegal

The residents of Yinghua Lane on Robison Road in western Shanghai are mostly from the lower classes, and many criminals mingle among them. Han Lijiang, a Jiangbei native, is one of them. He does not engage in honest work and is prone to stealing. On the 11th of this month, Han sneaked into a construction site on nearby Haifang Road and stole firewood. Wang Caifu and Lu Er, the gatekeepers, discovered this and dragged him back into the construction site, tied him up, and whipped him until he was covered in injuries and barely breathing. They then released him. Han, seriously injured, tried to return home, but collapsed on Binlang Road. Around noon last Saturday, a patrolman from the Gordon Road Police Station passed by and saw that he had been dead for some time. He reported to the head of the police station, who ordered a detective to carry the body to the forensic examination office on Fei Lun Road and investigate the situation. Wang and Lu were arrested. Yesterday morning, the Special District Court commissioned Prosecutor Xu to come to the office to verify the case. Han Zhangshi, the deceased's mother, who is over sixty-seven years old, arrived and claimed that her son was murdered by Wang and Lu and requested justice. Wang and Lu only admitted to tying Han to a wooden pillar with a rope. Prosecutor Xu stated that whether he was beaten to death should be determined after an autopsy. The body was handed over to the mother for coffin preparation and burial. Wang and Lu were detained pending trial in court.

Extortionist Arrested at Longmen Road Intersection 174

Liu Bomeng from Sichuan, residing at No. 680, Haige Road, western Shanghai, currently a bookkeeper at the Dachuantong Customs Brokerage on Jiujiang Road, suddenly received a threatening letter on the 10th of this month demanding 5,000 yuan. The location for delivering the money was arranged at the intersection of Dagu Road and Longmen Road, next to the racetrack. The money was to be placed on the edge of the curb, and someone would come to retrieve it. Liu reported this to the Jing'an Temple Police Station for investigation. He first replied to the letter, stating that he was currently experiencing economic difficulties and requested a reduction in the amount, which he might be able to manage. He placed the letter on the curb at the designated location. Liu and detectives lay in ambush nearby. Sure enough, someone came to retrieve the letter, and the detectives did not disturb him. On the 14th, Liu received another letter from the extortionist, saying that the previous letter had been read and that the amount had been reduced to 1,000 yuan, which must be delivered at the same location at 11 p.m. the next night. Liu reported this to the police station again. The head of the police station dispatched detectives Lang Jintang and Wang Yongjun, as well as detective Yu Changyuan, to wait there the following night. Liu first wrapped waste paper into a package and ordered Lu Er to accompany the detectives to place the package on the edge of the curb. Only ten minutes had passed when a boy came along, picked up the paper package, put it in his arms, turned around, and was arrested by the detectives. Yesterday morning, Liu, Lu, and others were brought to the Special District Court, where Judge Wu Tingqi presided over the hearing. The boy stated that his name was Lu Qinyu, 18 years old, from Tongzhou, and that he worked as a shop assistant at the Banxintai Wood Shop at No. 223, Hankou Road. Last night, a friend named Zhou asked him to go to that location to retrieve a paper package, and he did not know what was inside when he was arrested. The police lawyer then presented the threatening letters received by Liu as evidence and requested a postponement of the hearing. Judge Wu ordered the defendant to be detained and postponed the hearing to the morning of the 20th of this month.

Russian Red and White Pine Arrives in Shanghai 176

Managed by Gui Hongchang

The Russian red and white pine are suitable for construction factories and other factories such as organ frames and instrument factories. Because of their smooth texture, beautiful color, no knots, and ease of work, they were very popular in Shanghai in the past. Unfortunately, this product has been discontinued for many years, and users have been looking forward to it for a long time. Now, to meet the needs of society, the company has spent a lot of time and money and transported a large number of high-quality red and white pine to Shanghai. The goods have arrived in port and are exclusively managed by the Hongchang Wood Company on Guangfu Road, Zhabei.

Notice from the Traffic Department to Machine Vehicle Owners 177

Public Concession Police Department Traffic Department Circular

It has come to our attention that the sound of car horns causes annoyance. Please pay special attention to Article 30 of the Traffic Regulations: "Drivers are not allowed to use horns, bells, or other warning devices unless necessary, to avoid annoying the public." Please note and warn your drivers that the police will resolutely punish those who violate this regulation. Special warning: In the following circumstances, there is no need to use the horn: (1) In residential areas from 11 p.m. to 6 a.m. (2) At any time or place, unless clearly obstructed and there is a risk of danger to pedestrians or other vehicles, and unless the obstruction cannot be avoided even with reduced speed (in this case, only one or two short sounds are sufficient, and long or continuous sounds are prohibited). (3) At the door of any house to warn people inside. (4) On remote or sparsely populated roads. (5) To maintain or increase vehicle speed. Vehicles equipped with rubber bulb horns do not need to use electric horns unless in emergencies. If drivers drive according to Articles 20 and 21 of the Traffic Regulations, they will not only reduce the number of times they use the horn but also reduce the chances of causing accidents. All Traffic Regulations can be obtained in person or by letter from the Traffic Department free of charge. Public Concession Police Department Traffic Inspector, May 29, 1930.

Three Days as a Wife in the White Dove Show 180

Yang Yuhong Deceived into Marriage

Xu Amei, the Matchmaker, is Detained

Yang Yuhong from Wuxi, 30 years old, resides at No. 139, Guohuo Road, southern Shanghai, and works as a worker at the Qiuxin Machinery Factory. His wife, Zhou, passed away in August the year before last. Because Yang lacked someone to manage the household, he was thinking of remarrying. He met Xu Amei and Chen Wangshi, who offered to act as matchmakers. There was a Ningbo woman named Shu, 33 years old, with good looks, who was in difficult circumstances due to being alone and was planning to marry. Yang was delighted to hear this and paid 80 yuan as betrothal money. Later, he married Shu into his home. However, Shu's background was not proper, and she actually used the skills of a "white dove" to deceive people out of money. Therefore, only three days after entering the house on the 13th of this month, she took advantage of Yang's absence at work and secretly left yesterday morning, taking all the clothes and two sock machines. When Yang returned home, she was long gone, and he was extremely upset. He asked people to investigate everywhere, but there was no trace. He went to Chen Wangshi's house at No. 103, Wanghai Mound, Haichao Temple South Street, at 4 p.m., but she had already heard the news and fled. He twisted her paramour, Tang Abao, a local, and then went to Xu Amei, a matchmaker from Shaoxing, at No. 16, Sanduo Lane, and twisted her. He immediately called the guard Feng Junzhong from the 24th post of the precinct to bring them back to the Third Precinct, First District. The precinct chief, Jin, interrogated them and ordered them to be detained for investigation before further action.

Opening of the Child Welfare Health Clinic 181

The Health Clinic for Children of the China Child Welfare Association in Zhabei has moved from the Baptist Church to the end of Qiujiang Road in January. More than 4,000 people have benefited from it. Considering that the Yangshupu area is full of factories and residents, and that they are unable to protect the health and happiness of their children due to lack of knowledge or financial difficulties, the association has joined hands with Shanghai University and the Shanghai East Community to set up a Child Welfare Health Clinic at No. 1032, Linqing Road. It has hired famous Shanghai doctors such as Dr. Niu Huisheng and Dr. Fu Wenshou to preside over medical affairs, and there are female nurses providing all-day service. Promoting health and scheduled to open on June 20th, all consultations and medications are free of charge for children. If you have any questions regarding children's health, please contact the clinic at any time.

Regarding the Shi Ruiji Xin Xie Shun Housing Affair

The Luye Guild sends a telegram: To the Shanghai Special Municipality Party Department, the Party Departments of each district, the Municipal Government Social Bureau, the Commercial Consolidation Council, various industry associations, legal groups, and newspaper offices. Sincerely, according to a letter from our member Shi Ruiji Xin Xie Shun, a shop owner on Doushan Road, the landlord, Wen Xiao Company, sent a letter in the name of the Municipal North Inspection Office, claiming to be acting on the orders of the Municipal Government and intending to rent our shop for use as an office, and claiming to be opening a bank, repeatedly threatening and urging us to move, and saying that construction would begin after the 15th of this month. We have repeatedly pleaded, but to no avail. From then on, our business has nowhere to go and nothing to do. Therefore, we request assistance and come to ask you to take measures to stop this. Upon review, the company, etc., belongs to a small merchant. In 16 years, it was looted and burned by the Fengjun army. After that, it worked hard to operate until now. The original spirit has not recovered, and there is a sudden occurrence of mandatory rental and forced relocation, making it impossible for it to survive, which is very painful. How can today's officials bear to do this? I am afraid that there will inevitably be those who engage in economic aggression to fool and oppress small merchants to achieve their desires. The landlord is manipulated by them, so he dares to act recklessly, which not only hinders the interests of our members, but also violates the principles of the Premier's livelihood. Therefore, we specially telegraph the situation and ask you to uphold justice and provide assistance to rescue the oppressed merchants and relieve their suffering. We cannot express our anticipation and gratitude enough. We respectfully telegraph and await your high voice. Shanghai Special Municipality Luye Guild, June 15th.

Weather Report 188

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:20 PM yesterday stated that the skies over the Yangtze River basin and the Shandong coastal area were mostly cloudy, while the skies in the south were overcast. The winds along the coast of the country were directionless. There was a low-pressure area northwest of Yap Island in the Pacific Ocean, which might form a low-pressure center. Also, within the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday, the highest temperature in the city was 80.6 degrees, and the lowest was 6.44 degrees. On the same day last year, the highest was 76.0 degrees, and the lowest was 67.8 degrees.
