Free Talk

Just a Laugh Hai Ke 189

A: I've been researching spiritualism recently. Do you know how old the oldest ghost is?

B: How would I know? Why don't you check your own family tree?

Husband: I've been ordered by the company to go to the branch offices in various commercial ports to investigate business conditions. I'll be back in a month.

Wife: It's alright. I have a date with my girlfriends to travel and I'll be back in two months.

Old Man: Doctor, my daughter suddenly fainted this morning. Although she woke up, she's in a daze, as if she's lost her senses.

Doctor: Don't worry. There are many people like that in the world, some are like that for their entire lives.

Judge: You are extremely guilty and should be sentenced to three years and six months in prison.

Criminal: I'm deaf and can't hear what the official is saying.

Judge: You were clearly not deaf just now. How can you say you're deaf now?

Criminal: My ears go deaf when they hear unpleasant words. If you don't want me to be deaf, please say something pleasant.

Mourning Mr. Yu Tiansui Zhao Mianyun 190

Mr. Yu Tiansui of Kunshan died in Shanghai. All his friends are mourning him. My sworn brother Zheng Yimei wrote an article describing his life and friendship. I also admired Mr. Tiansui. I heard that Mr. Yu abandoned his old residence and lived in Shanghai for nearly 20 years because of debt. Although he was poor and had no possessions, he was generous and righteous and often helped people in need. I heard this from Mr. Hu Shiyu a few years ago. Mr. Yu was a top student of Mr. Shiyu. Recently, I inquired about any elegiac works. He wrote and sent four elegiac poems. I was moved and recorded them in Free Talk for those who knew Mr. Tiansui to read. The zodiac sign is like a scorpion, and one's fate is sad. Selling the house to ghosts causes suffering. Living abroad is costly. The writing is extremely passionate, and life is disjointed. A haggard, homeless traveler, where will the wandering soul rest? Recalling when he went to war as a secretary. His talent moved the old poet (Jingyun had a poem about joining the army). Poetic affairs were sent with letters. Green wine stained his sleeves, and he leaned on the painted boat on the red bridge (Your poem has the line "Joining the army all day is idle, on the red bridge above the painted boat"). I can't bear to look back. The old dreams are like smoke. He was righteous and chivalrous, considering wealth lightly. He was talented in many arts (He was skilled in calligraphy, painting, seal carving, and medicine). His spirit was free. He roamed the rivers and lakes alone. He cherished old friends. Naturally, everyone sighed with regret. In the wind and rain, the rooster crowed. Many relatives and friends lamented the loss of the orphan. Home studies should be protected, lest the books be unread. Without good seedlings, bad weeds will grow. Good men will rise like reeds. Letting go ten years early is a great difficulty for the future. Alas!

One-Finger Zen Monk and Female Student Wang Meiqu 191

Mr. Yin Yucai is proficient in Buddhism and lives in the Shanghai Lay Buddhist Forest, eating vegetarian food often and meat rarely. Last Tuesday, I met him at Mr. Wu Yingsheng's house in Zhenqing Lane.

Common Sense for Small Employees Jiang Xinqing 192

When you first arrive, avoid unnecessary small talk with colleagues, as they will use this to test your abilities.

When you first arrive, do not work too hard, as excessive effort will both provoke jealousy from peers and cause dissatisfaction from superiors if you cannot sustain it.

Be amiable to subordinates (or those younger than you), respectful to those at your level, and courteous to superiors. Apart from fulfilling your duties, keep personal feelings at a distance.

If your superior asks you to do personal favors, never show an eager attitude, or someone will say you are flattering them, creating a hostile environment.

In your spare time, avoid excessive idle talk or commenting on any matters.

When chatting and laughing with colleagues, be very careful, as gossip often arises from such conversations.

Sell your talent if you can, but do not overexpose it, because if you truly have talent, there will be opportunities to sell it.

True friends are hard to find. Those who are with you all the time are not necessarily true friends. Be careful.

During drinks, Yucai mentioned many ancient and modern Buddhist scriptures. Finally, he mentioned a recent incident. I was half drunk and didn't remember much, only that there was a female student who became a monk. At 6:00 PM on the 13th, Mr. Yingsheng invited me for drinks and food, and I met Yucai again. I quickly asked him for details while I was still sober and recorded them to document the strangeness. There is a monk named Yuexi who is currently in charge of the Yuantong Temple in Hongkou, Shanghai. His virtue is highly respected, and he is revered as a Vajra Master. Recently, several female students came to bow and take refuge, wishing to be accepted as disciples. The monk said, "Excellent! Buddha is mind, and mind is Buddha. All of you young ladies are studying and have responsibilities to your families and the country. I fear this is not the time for monastic life. Entering into tranquility and samadhi cannot be decided lightly on a whim." The female students all vowed that they had no other intentions and insisted on shaving their heads. The monk said again, "There is a bhikshuni (female monastic) elsewhere who is no ordinary person. If you insist, you can go to her." After the monk said this, the others were silent. One female student went straight to the kitchen. In a moment, she held out a finger to the monk and said, "Disciple has already cut off this finger." She also showed it to her companions, saying, "There is no blood under the knife." The monk then folded his hands and proclaimed the Buddha's name, also raising his hand to show the assembly that he had also cut off a whisk in the past to resolve his determination to pursue monastic life. Yucai said this much. I said, "The mantle has unexpectedly been passed on to a female Bodhisattva in Buddhism, who must be no ordinary being. But what is her name, surname, home, and school?" I hope you can tell me. Yucai said he didn't know, only that he heard that Buddhism does not allow lying. I also asked about the other students who were worshiping, but he did not know the details. Daohu brother laughed and said, "This is truly practicing One-Finger Zen!" Daohu is the intelligent son of Yingsheng, my esteemed friend, and he is especially close to Yucai.

A Bizarre Suicide Case Huang Yingdai 193

Recently, the town of Chonggu, which was looted by bandits, is located north of Qingpu. A bizarre suicide case occurred near the town a few days ago. The situation is quite interesting, both sad and laughable, so I record it.

Beautiful Nun. There is a nunnery in a village near Chonggu. A nun named Doukou is young and beautiful, and her behavior is quite lively, with absolutely no air of a religious person. Therefore, many frivolous young men drooled over her. When they saw her go out, they followed her. The occurrence of this suicide case was probably due to the nun's beauty.

Raped. A few days ago, this beautiful nun went out for something. When she was returning to the nunnery, she was walking alone on a path between the fields. At that time, she suddenly encountered a rogue who saw her beauty and wanted to rape her. The nun looked around and there was no one. Even if she shouted for help, it would be ineffective. At this critical moment, she came up with a clever plan and pretended to agree to let the rogue take off her lower garments. The rogue did not suspect anything, thinking that something good would happen. Unexpectedly, the nun took the opportunity to run away. The rogue lay on the ground, got up to chase, but it was too late.

Borrowed Trousers. After the nun escaped from the rogue, she ran to the center of a nearby small village and finally felt a little safer. However, because her lower garments were still in the field, she felt very uncomfortable walking naked. So she entered a farmer's house to hide temporarily. A woman in the farmer's house asked her what happened and finally learned the details. So she borrowed her own trousers. In the evening, the nun returned to the nunnery.

Mistaken Monk. As the sun set, the farmer's husband returned from working in the fields. Because of the hot weather, he was covered in sweat, so he drew water to bathe. After bathing, he changed his clothes and looked for his trousers but could not find them. He asked his wife and learned that she had mistakenly given her husband's trousers to the nun in a hurry. His five-year-old son said, "A monk came to our house, and my mother treated him with refreshments. He borrowed a pair of trousers before leaving." The child could not distinguish between right and wrong and thought the bald-headed nun was a monk.

Three Lives Lost Together. When the farmer heard this, he thought his wife was having an affair with a monk. Unable to contain his anger, he wanted to kill his wife. His wife could not defend herself, and in despair, she hanged herself that night. The next day, the nun who borrowed the trousers returned the original pair. Seeing the scene, she was shocked and told the farmer the whole story. When the farmer learned that it was a misunderstanding, he was filled with regret and took his own life in extreme pain. The nun, feeling that she had caused the loss of two lives, could not bear it and also committed suicide with a knife. Thus, three people died together. The groundless rumor arose from a child's word. It is said that the child has now been taken in by relatives.

Publishing News. Since the publication of Jia Shan Ye Jinqiu's new book, "Analysis of Zhongjing's Theory," it has been praised by Chinese medicine schools in China as an extremely outstanding work of the century. It has made great contributions to Chinese medicine. Professors from Chinese medicine schools in Taiwan, Fujian, Zhejiang, and other places have contacted the publishing house to purchase copies for teaching. It is said that the first edition has already sold out. The copyright belongs to the Sheng Nian Chinese Medicine Society at No. 78 Yuqingfang, North Sichuan Road.

Warmth in the Heart (214) Bao Tianxiao 194

Chapter 12: A farewell banquet with flowers to leave a beautiful memory. A grand gathering in the garden to compare tea and view the beautiful scenery.

Zuo Shichen actually finished all his work for the day while making the phone call. When A Jin replied on the phone that they would arrive at 7:30, there was still an hour and a half to go. Going too early would be boring, so he wanted to take advantage of this free time to spread out his manuscript and write something. He seriously wrote only two lines and then put the manuscript away. He walked over to Liu Xing's desk where he was translating Western texts and talked to him. He said that there was no news in the Western newspapers today. "I'm almost done with my work. Let's go eat at a small restaurant." Zuo Shichen said, "I have another appointment today." Fearing that Liu Xing would ask him who was hosting, he walked away. He went to stand on the balcony on the third floor and saw that the electric lights on the left, right, front, and back were already on. The noisy sounds of singing mixed with the sounds of vehicles on the road were playing a symphony. The outlines of the tall buildings were dissolved into a sea of light. He walked back in and lingered until the clock on the wall struck seven. He went to Yizhixiang first. He thought that their timing could not be accurate. Even if they said they would arrive at 7:30, perhaps there would be a performance at Yizhixiang, so he came early to serve them first. It took three minutes for the rickshaw to run from Wangping Street to Yizhixiang on the crowded Fuzhou Road. When he walked up the stairs of Yizhixiang and looked at the big clock opposite, it hadn't struck seven yet. The long hand was pointing at 56 minutes. Zuo Shichen thought that the clocks in Shanghai probably had the time of the whole world, but he didn't know whose time was correct. In short, people always made progress within this time. When he went up the stairs, a waiter came to greet him and took him to the small room. There was a certain prelude. First, two hot towels were sent up. Sometimes they were so hot that they burned. Some people said that Chinese people's skin was burned old by these hot towels, so young girls don't need that kind of hot towel. The towel was handed up and they never wiped their faces. At most, they wiped their hands. It doesn't matter if they're old hands. It's still a good noun in Chinese society! After wiping with the hot towel, a cup of tea was immediately served. Ordinary guests were served tea in a covered bowl. Regular customers were treated preferentially by the waiters and served in a long glass cup. They specially brewed a cup of tea. There was black tea and sugar cubes. There was green tea with a few tea leaves floating on top and gradually sinking. Zuo Shichen was favored by the white-clothed waiters. In addition to the red and green teas, they sent him a cup of lemon tea. A slice of lemon floated in the glass cup like a wheel, and a lot of sugar was added. It looked lightly colored, but when you drank it, it was sweet and sour, just like today's situation.

Qingfeng Yuan Di

Correspondence Regarding the Difficult Play Movement 211

Mr. Editor,

The following is a brief report on our Difficult Play Movement before and after its execution. Please grant us a small space in the artistic world to announce this to the public, and we hope to receive guidance and assistance from those who generally love drama.

(I) Motivation for Holding the Difficult Play Movement

It can be said that there are two motivations for us to hold this Difficult Play Movement. The first is the loss incurred on May 10th and 11th. We know ourselves that our audience is more than this. We thought it must have been affected by the tram strike. Therefore, we wanted to revive "Uncle Vanya" at the same time. Afraid that one performance of "Uncle Vanya" would not be able to recover our costs, we decided to add "The Dog's Dance" and "Peach Blossom Spring". The second motivation is because the general audience who have seen our "Peach Blossom Spring" still mention it from time to time. Therefore, we think this play is worth performing again. At the same time, some people have been encouraging us to revive "The Dog's Dance" because it only played for one day last year. So we decided to revive three plays at the same time. Because these three plays are all recognized as difficult plays, we regarded these three plays as a systematic Difficult Play Movement.

(II) Planned Repertoire

In our dedication, we have already explained clearly that our original repertoire was like this: the first sound of the movement was "The Dog's Dance," the second sound was "Uncle Vanya," and the third sound was "Peach Blossom Spring," from despair to hope, from hope to action. However, because several characters in "The Dog's Dance" and "Uncle Vanya" are played by the same actors, we feared the loss of individuality. We had to perform "Uncle Vanya" first. There were other reasons, so we had to change our ideal repertoire.

(III) Various Difficulties During the Movement

(1) The Fewness of the Audience: On the day of the revival of "Uncle Vanya" on the 31st, we found that our audience was even smaller than before. So we understood that we had lost our original audience. Because of this reason, many members were as discouraged as the Peach Fairies in the second act of Peach Blossom Spring. Fortunately, we still had hermit-like members who encouraged each other to complete this movement.

(2) Loss of Helpers: We know very well that the reason why we lost our audience is because the plays we perform are too profound and too dull. At the same time, the internal members also did not feel interested and scattered. For this large movement, we only had about twenty people in total, which makes us proud and heartbroken. (3) Changes in Staff and Actors: At a time when there were so few people, our business manager Hong Chengfu and set director Wu Senkang had to return to Ningbo due to family matters until the 6th before returning to Shanghai. Our important actors Luo Mingfeng and Tang Yuanfan also resigned from their tasks, one due to important professional matters, and the other due to the Fudan performance of "Cyrano de Bergerac." Therefore, our organization was somewhat chaotic, and the division of powers could not be clearly defined. At the same time, the staff and actors on the stage could not concentrate on preparing for the play and helping with the work in the front of the house.

(4) Difficulties in Rehearsing: Among the three plays in this movement, "Uncle Vanya" was rehearsed well, but "The Dog's Dance" was a year ago, and "Peach Blossom Spring" was more than two years ago, and many roles had to be changed, so it had to be rehearsed again. However, we simply could not spare much time. For "Peach Blossom Spring," we completely sacrificed one night of sleep on the evening of the 7th to rehearse it.

(5) Economic Embarrassment: Outsiders usually feel that our theater troupe is very financially sufficient. Yes, according to our expenses, it does look very wealthy. However, this money is only spent on the stage. Not to mention that staff and actors do not dare to have extravagant enjoyment, even the advertising money is very stingy. Naturally, compared to poorer theater troupes, we seem to have much more strength. But precisely because of this, we want to do our best to make more perfect contributions in stage technology. But we were too bold. This time our loss may exceed one thousand. Now there is still a large amount of debt unpaid. If we cannot handle it properly within this week, we may end up in an unimaginable situation.

(IV) Results of the Movement

(1) The Outside World's View of Us: Although we had very few audiences this time, these were all eliminated. They are all audiences who truly support us and love our dramas. So they are satisfied with our movement this time. Also, the literary and artistic circles have expressed their satisfaction with us verbally.

(2) Our View of the Outside World This Time: We are very grateful to the outside world, not because of their praise of us, but because of their sincere corrections to us. We have accepted everything possible. Also, Chun Jun, who criticized our "Peach Blossom Spring" in Shen Bao, and Chun Sen Jun, who criticized our "Uncle Vanya" in the Min Guo Daily, I don't know if it is the same person or who it is. He has great hope for our future. We are grateful to him. We will always endure hardships like Miss Qin, and persevere like the Peach Fairies, so as not to disappoint him.

(3) Our Own View of Ourselves: Although the outside world has expressed satisfaction with our movement this time, we are all very regretful. Everyone's face shows a somewhat dissatisfied expression, because the shortcomings are only the clearest to ourselves. None of us have achieved our ideals. On this point, we can tell the comrades who care about us that we seem to still have hope of moving forward.

(4) The Representative Plays of This Movement: Drama is a comprehensive art. Everyone knows how complicated the organization inside is. As long as one staff member or actor makes a mistake, the whole play will be ruined. This time, because of the lack of manpower and the busyness of affairs, our play could not be like a machine, always the same (we used to be like this). There were several times when we really did not dare to admit it was our play. However, among the six performances of "Vanya," we admit the two performances of The Dog's Dance on the morning of May 10th, the two performances of Peach Blossom Spring on the morning of June 7th, and the performance on the evening of the 8th. We admit that these three performances are the representative plays of our movement this time.

(V) Our Future

(1) To Get Back Our Audience and Our Helpers: Our first thing to do in the future is to find a way to get back our original audience and helpers. Our specialization in difficult plays is our success, but we have failed because of this. Our audience and helpers are also our failures. Therefore, we must find a way to get them back.

(2) Our Future Policy: When Chinese drama is just sprouting, when the audience is not yet interested in and does not believe in new dramas, and when we have not yet grasped the psychology of the Beijing opera audience, it is also a wrong policy to perform these difficult plays. Therefore, we must change our policy in the future and perform plays that are more sympathetic to the audience or more accessible plays. However, we hope that those who care about us will not be pessimistic about us. We want to set up elementary schools and think about dividing them into periods, just like dividing them into classes, and proceed in sequence.

(3) Internal Reorganization: Mr. Zhu Suicheng has a very good plan to change our organization and divide it into viewing group members and working group members. Normally, there should be frequent training to improve the dramatic level of the viewers and workers. Now this proposal is only a private discussion among everyone. After these matters are all settled, we will submit it to the committee for detailed discussion. After a decision is made, there will naturally be progress. Xin You Theater Troupe, June 14th, 19th year.

Qualification Issues and University Education 212

Dear Reader,

I would very much like to discuss this issue with you, but because I am burdened with affairs, I rush through the day. Today, I am finally able to write. The motivation for me to discuss this issue is that two months ago, when the National Education Conference opened, a reporter from the Shanghai Times News published an article in his newspaper discussing current university education. I read it and had some thoughts. Later, this article was reprinted by the Tianjin Guo Wen Weekly (I forgot which issue). The fact that this article is worth noting is undoubtedly undeniable. The gist of this article is (because I don't have this newspaper on hand, it is inconvenient to check, so I can only write the general idea):

"The level of current university education is too low. It has regressed compared to when schools were first established, and there is a sense of decline. Taking the tool of learning - writing - as an example, in the past, university students, in addition to their native language, had at least two or three foreign languages. What about today's university students? Not to mention that they cannot master foreign languages, even their native language is not as good as that of middle and primary school students in the past. Some even cannot write an ordinary letter fluently. Therefore, the urgent task now is to enrich the content of university courses and improve the level of university education."

The meaning of this article is to show the current state of university education and to urge current education authorities and people in society to pay attention to it. From this, it can be seen that the shallowness of the level of university education is a very obvious fact, and the fact that knowledgeable people in society regard it as a disease is "everyone thinks the same, everyone feels the same." However, let's think about why the level of current university education is lower than before. There should be a reason. If we find this reason, we will be able to prescribe the right medicine. Otherwise, no matter what method you use to reform, it will not work. However, the so-called reason is of course several kinds. What we want to find is the most fundamental reason. So I did some investigation. What is the fundamental reason for the shallowness of the level of current university education? Unexpectedly, the thing that I immediately thought of was "qualification." I dare to argue that "if the issue of qualification is not broken one day, the level of university education cannot be improved one day." However, when the "qualification issue" is deeply rooted and unbreakable in today's politics and education, people will definitely think that this kind of argument is made by a madman. Therefore, the qualification issue and university education must be discussed in detail. The reason for the poor level of university education, according to the shallow speculation of ordinary people, is generally thought to lie in the fact that there are too many students who have studied in the East and the West and returned to China. There are too many new bureaucrats and frustrated politicians in the past few years. Students who have studied abroad have nothing to do, so they want to run universities. Bureaucrats and politicians want to gain false fame and win over students, so they also want to run universities. These two kinds of people all want to run universities, so wild chicken universities are everywhere. The motivation for establishing wild chicken universities is fundamentally not concerned with education, so they indiscriminately enroll students, the equipment is simple, and the professors are sloppy. As a result, how can the level of students not be shallow? Since there are many wild chicken universities, students don't have to worry about not having a place to go to school. As a result, it also affects middle school students not paying much attention to their homework. Since the level of middle school is poor, how can the level of university not be shallow? As a result, the level of non-wild chicken universities is also shallow. Therefore, the way to improve the level of university education is to shut down wild chicken universities. I think the reason for this kind of speculation is superficial. Although I relatively agree with this method of improving the level of university education, it is not fundamental. Let's think further. The reason why there are so many wild chicken universities is, of course, that students who have studied abroad have nothing to do, and that bureaucrats and politicians want to sell their reputation, fish for fame, and win over students as their genes. But every time I ask, wild chicken universities always have more than three or five hundred students. There are so many people going to university. What is the reason for this? Today's university students - especially those in wild chicken universities - spend at least five hundred yuan a year. Their fathers and brothers are naturally not all capitalists. Are they willing to give so much of their hard-earned money to their children to spend? The level of today's universities is unreliable. Don't they all understand this? However, the number of people who painstakingly provide their children to go to university is increasing day by day. There must be a reason for this. There is no need to say that it is difficult to live in society today. Without a university degree, one cannot obtain a decent position in society. Especially if you want to be an official, you cannot rise to prominence without a university degree. If you want to be promoted, of course, this example is not included, but there will also be criticism of "personal favoritism." That is, future national examinations also require a university diploma to be eligible to take the exam. Therefore, it can be summarized in one sentence: "The purpose of today's fathers and brothers providing their children to go to university is for "qualification." The purpose of students going to university to study is also for "qualification." Everything else outside of qualification is not a very important issue. Then how can the level of university education not be shallow? Also, because the purpose of students studying is only to obtain "qualification," professors with knowledge often have such a sigh: "I teach so hard, but I am just creating diplomas for them. Why bother?" Students whose real purpose is not to learn but to obtain "qualification" request to be exempt from exams, reduce the number of questions, issue more handouts, and read fewer reference books. It is indeed too uncomfortable for knowledgeable professors. Therefore, those with a little money do not want to teach at universities, and today's university education is built on the students' diplomas and the teachers' salaries. My university students and professors have agreed with this statement. How can the level of university education not be shallower? From this, everyone can make a fair judgment: is the fundamental reason for the low level of university education the establishment of many wild chicken universities, or is it the importance that the general public in society attaches to the issue of qualification? We can answer immediately: if the general public does not have a need for qualification, then wild universities

Page 26

chicken universities will absolutely not be able to operate successfully. The reason for the low level of university education lies entirely in the importance that the general public in society attaches to the issue of qualification. Attributing the low level of university education to wild chicken universities is a superficial theory and is putting the cart before the horse. Therefore, to improve the level of university education, we must first break the issue of qualification. That is, the kind of talent that society needs must go through national examinations. This kind of examination should absolutely not be limited to qualification. We must take into account his daily cultivation. As long as he is given a rigorous examination, the awarding of degrees will be the same. Then the level of university education will naturally be improved. (Qie Xiang)

A Few Thought-Provoking Words by Ge Zimi 213

Nanyang Middle School, which has been operating in Shanghai for more than 30 years, recently held its spring sports meet at the China Athletics Field. Hundreds of athletes competed on the green lawn to show their good skills. Among them, four records were broken, setting new school records. It is commendable that secondary schools have achieved such good results. The new records are as follows:

100 meters (Huang Guanxiong) Record: 11.3 seconds

1500 meters (Liang Yanping) Record: 4 minutes and 32 seconds

Low Hurdles (Huang Chengliang) Record: 28 seconds

Discus (Pan Risheng) Record: 25.68 meters

On June 12, the school held an awards ceremony for the winners in the school's alumni hall. Teachers, alumni, guests, and students attended, totaling more than a thousand people. The prizes were extremely rich. The awards were presented by Mr. Gu Tianfang, the school's director of studies. Mr. Gu recently returned to China from Japan, where he observed overseas Chinese education. He gave a speech of about half an hour at the meeting. His words were pertinent and thought-provoking, and could be regarded as golden rules in this period when physical education is urgently needed. Here are a few excerpts for the consideration of the gentlemen of the world.

"When I visited various primary and secondary schools in Japan, I saw that their school buildings, even those with great reputations, were shallow and dilapidated, with very few tall halls and buildings. The sports fields were not very large either. This is because Japan is small and densely populated, so it cannot be otherwise. Since the sports fields are small, the practice time must be rotated so that some students can avoid being left out. Although the practice time is short, the reason why their results are excellent is because they have perseverance. Compared to the ordinary schools in Japan, our sports fields are more than adequate. Gentlemen, please do not miss such a great opportunity.

In Japan, it is rare to see people with fair complexions like us. This is because people like to exercise and exercise in the sunlight, which turns them black. Over time, people have also shifted their aesthetic concepts to regard black as a symbol of health and love it deeply. From this, we can see the general national character. How does this compare to our country's worship of "fair-faced scholars"?

Japanese people, regardless of gender, age, or size, like to exercise. They often play ball and kick ball on the small roads next to their houses after work. How does this compare to our countrymen who play mahjong and smoke cigarettes in their free time?

Japanese people have perseverance and perseverance in sports, unlike our country's athletes who are exposed to the sun for one day and then cold for ten days. In the Far East Games, the Japanese have long wanted to win the football title. Therefore, they practiced desperately and did not hesitate to send players to the United States to learn new methods at great expense. In terms of technology, our country has indeed made progress, but only knows how to stick to the old methods. Therefore, when the Japanese side used a new formula during the war, our country's players were confused. Although the Japanese could not win the entire championship, they were able to vent their anger for a while.

Gentlemen, you are young and strong. Please work hard in order to win glory for the country in the future. This is my sincere hope."

A Letter Worthy of Attention 214

Discussing the Issue of Transferring Schools

"You know me, right? I am the most protective of our school. Although everything in our school cannot completely satisfy people, it can still be considered the best among the wild chicken universities in Shanghai. Just talking about the law department, the director is concurrently held by the president of the school, who is a doctor of law. Half of the professors are professors from the Soochow University Law School, and half are judges and prosecutors from the Provisional Court. It can be said that it is a gathering of talents from the Shanghai legal community. New students cannot be arbitrarily inserted into classes, and students in school cannot be absent from classes without reason. On these few points, we often boast that our school's law department is the second law school of Soochow University. We can study in such a school without having to think about going abroad to seek higher education and quietly wait for graduation. But the problem comes.

The biggest problem we have, I think you understand, is the issue of the school's registration. We know that a student studying law whose diploma is not from a national university or a private university law school that has been registered by the Ministry of Education and recognized by the Judicial Yuan, then the diploma he or she gets is equal to a piece of waste paper. It is not legally effective. You cannot take the judicial examination to become a judge or a lawyer. The school authorities of our school also feel the importance of this issue. Therefore, in the last semester, they have been working hard to raise funds and purchase a base. However, although the school base has been purchased, covering fifty acres, there is still no good news about the construction of the school building after a semester. I dare to say that our school only needs to build a school building to be registered by the Ministry of Education, and the recognition of the Ministry of Justice is even less of a problem. Alas, the school building is a prerequisite for registration. Why don't the school authorities rush to proceed to comfort the hopes of all the students? Isn't the law school on Jiangwan Road adding school buildings, which our classmates have all seen with their own eyes? Touching the scenery, what should we feel?

Brother Jian, I personally absolutely cherish our school, but my parents are forcing me to transfer schools, saying that if I don't transfer schools, I will cut off my way out. Smart Brother Jian, do you think it is better to wait for our school to be registered in the future, or is it better to transfer schools immediately? Assuming I transfer schools, the best law school in Shanghai is of course Soochow, but my English level is not high enough. Then which school should I transfer to? Please give me some advice."

The above is a letter written to me by a classmate. Our school's law department is not bad, this is a fact. As for transferring schools, except for Soochow, it is inevitable to degrade the requirements. The school authorities are not doing their best to proceed with the registration, this is also a fact. If I don't transfer schools, it is inevitable to suffer a loss in my own way out. I really cannot answer this question. However, I believe that our school can definitely build a school building and be registered within two years. Once the school is registered, the graduated students will also receive the same benefits. Therefore, if there is no other reason to transfer schools at present, or if there is no suitable school to transfer to for the time being, it is better not to transfer. I replied to my classmate with this intention.

I also feel that there must be not a few students in Shanghai who have transferred schools due to the school registration issue. But it can be understood by looking at the large number of transfer students absorbed by the registered schools every semester. Therefore, I published this classmate's letter to show that the school's inability to register temporarily is also one of the reasons for students' transfer, and it is worthy of everyone's attention.

CUHK Hexapoecia Society 215

I have already introduced all the literary and academic societies in CUHK in this column. Now let me talk about its research associations. Speaking of its research associations, the most notable one is the Hexapoecia Society. The Hexapoecia Society, translated into Chinese, is the Six-Legged Society. This association is organized by students of the Department of Plant Pathology and Entomology of the College of Agriculture of CUHK and staff of the Jiangsu Provincial Entomology Bureau (the Jiangsu Entomology Bureau is located on the CUHK campus, so when people talk about the Heaxpoecia Society, they say it is the CUHK Hexapoecia Society. Please forgive me for also referring to it as the CUHK Hexapoecia Society here). It is dedicated to connecting emotions and researching entomology (especially locusts). It was announced in September and October of the year before last (the 17th year). It is said that the reason why it is named Heaxpoecia is because its purpose is to study entomology, especially locusts, and locusts have six legs, so they named it after six legs. (Xian Rong)

CUHK Law School Students Will 216

Organize a Social Survey Society 217

A few students in the CUHK Law School believe that studying law, politics, and economics cannot be effectively achieved by using textbooks in a dead way. Therefore, they also follow the example of those who study physics, chemistry, biology, and medicine by conducting experiments and organizing field surveys and investigations. It is heard that their procedures for organizing field surveys and investigations are to start by organizing a social survey society. The content is roughly divided into three points: (1) Engage in folk surveys to collect actual data on society. (2) Select problems that must be solved from the actual data. (3) Study each problem separately before gathering to debate. (Xian Rong)

Tobacco and alcohol tax is a major source of revenue for our country. Since the establishment of the special tax in the Qing Dynasty, it has been a long time, and the reforms and benefits have been extremely complicated. However, there is still a lack of specialized writings in the public and private sectors. The Tax Office has specially set up a Tobacco and Alcohol Tax Affairs Committee to edit the History of Tobacco and Alcohol Tax. The content is divided into ten chapters, including the evolution, region, tax system, public sales fee, tobacco and alcohol tax license tax, cigarette tax, foreign wine tax, revenue and expenditure overview, and rectification overview. It describes all the tax rule changes since the establishment and the current system, which is extremely comprehensive. At the end, an appendix is added, which includes the latest tax systems and tax rates of various countries in the East and the West, as well as the annual almanacs of tobacco and alcohol affairs, which are very detailed. It is truly a masterpiece in the financial world. The upper volume has been printed and sold. Now the lower volume has also been published, which is still entrusted to the Dadong Bookstore for sale. The price is three yuan for hardcover and two yuan and six jiao for paperback. The upper and lower volumes are all sold at 20% discount, etc.
